In re Terry E.


No. F005862


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


180 Cal. App. 3d 932; 225 Cal. Rptr. 803; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1563



May 9, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied July 24, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Stansilaus County, No. 191196, Norman S. Reid, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Stansilaus County (California), which declared her children free from her custody and control and which referred the children for adoption under Cal. Civ. Code § 232(a)(2) and (4). The order followed a juvenile court finding that they were dependent children within the meaning of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 300(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother's three children were placed in foster care in 1981 after her arrest and subsequent conviction for felonies associated with her and her boyfriend's kidnapping and sexual abuse of boyfriend's estranged wife. Appellant was serving a prison sentence for those crimes when respondent county welfare department sought to terminate her parent-child relationship with the children. The trial court terminated the parental relationship under Cal. Civ. Code § 232(a)(2) & (4). The court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court found the evidence was insufficient to support the termination. No reasonable trier of fact could find that the conditions which gave rise to appellant's cruelty and neglect of her children still existed when her parental rights were terminated. The court also found that her felony conviction was not sufficient grounds for termination. Respondent failed to prove that appellant had not or could not be rehabilitated during incarceration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which declared appellant mother's children free from her custody and control and which referred the children for adoption. The court found insufficient evidence to support the termination of appellant's parental rights, and the court concluded that any cruelty that may have existed in 1981 did not exist by 1985 and that appellant's felony conviction was not sufficient grounds for termination.

 

857 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Lewis


No. E001347


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


180 Cal. App. 3d 816; 225 Cal. Rptr. 782; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1552



May 6, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied July 23, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. VCR-2797, Donald R. Egan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which convicted defendant of a lesser included offense of involuntary manslaughter in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 192, and a firearm allegation was found to be true. Defendant claimed his conviction was barred by the three-year statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by information with murder in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 187, but was convicted of the lesser-included offense of involuntary manslaughter, Cal. Penal Code § 192. Defendant argued that the action was barred by the statute of limitations, the prosecution improperly impeached a defense witness, and it was error to impose the upper term sentence. On review the court found that at the time of the offense, the statute of limitation for manslaughter was three years, and because the pleadings failed to show some bar to the limitation, the conviction was jurisdictionally defective. The court held however that the error was not prejudicial and did not require reversal because the issuance of the arrest warrant shortly after the offense tolled the limitations period as a matter of law. The court held that application did not violate the ex post facto clause because a law that increased a limitations period or provided a new method of tolling it could have been immediately applied to all crimes, as long the period had not yet run under the prior law. The court rejected defendant's other arguments and affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because an arrest warrant was issued shortly after the date of the offense that tolled the statute of limitation as a matter of law. The court held that the ex post facto clause was not violated because laws that increased a limitations period applied to all crimes so long as the period had not run under the prior law.

Trailer Train Co. v. State Bd. of Equalization


Nos. A021208, A027732


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


180 Cal. App. 3d 565; 225 Cal. Rptr. 717; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1530



April 30, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 28, 1986, and Appellant's Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied August 13, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Nos. 769068, 742782, 764083, 782272, and 787740, Stuart R. Pollak and Robert W. Merrill, Judges.



DISPOSITION: We have thoroughly reviewed each issue Trailer Train raised in both appeals and we find no merit in any of them. The judgments are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant train company challenged the adverse judgment against them from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which was in favor of respondent state board of equalization in a cause of action brought by appellant for refunds on taxes assessed by respondent pursuant to the Private Railroad Car Tax Law (PRCTL), Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 11401, on appellant's fleet of flatcars.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state board of equalization annually assessed and levied a property tax on appellant train company's fleet of flatcars pursuant to the Private Railroad Car Tax Law (PRCTL), Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 11401. Appellant filed suit for refunds for tax years 1977 and 1980. Each suit claimed appellant was exempt from the PRCTL, that only the income method of valuation should have applied, that respondent's findings were not supported by substantial evidence, that respondent's procedures did not comport with due process, and that respondent's action resulted in multiple taxation. The trial court rendered judgment for respondent. In consolidated appeals, appellant challenged the adverse trial court rulings that upheld respondent's acts of levying an escape assessment by disallowing a claim for functional obsolescence and refusing to use only the income capitalization method to value appellant's fleet of flatcars for the tax years 1977 through 1980 under the PRCTL. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that appellant's flatcar fleet was not exempt from the PRCTL and that the legislature intended for flatcars to be included within the scope of the PRCTL.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court upholding respondent state board of equalization's act of levying an escape assessment and use of the income capitalization method to value appellant train company's fleet of flatcars because appellant's flatcar fleet was not exempt from the statute permitting escape tax assessment and both the constitution and statute required respondent to levy the escape assessment.

Thompson v. Bd. of Supervisors


No. A031603


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


180 Cal. App. 3d 555; 225 Cal. Rptr. 640; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1529



April 30, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 590467-5, Winton McKibben, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant voters sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which denied appellants' application for a writ of mandate seeking to compel respondent Board of Supervisors and Registrar of Voters of Alameda County to act upon appellants' referendum petition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant voters filed a writ of mandate seeking to compel respondent Board of Supervisors and Registrar of Voters of Alameda County to adopt an ordinance, which would repeal a redistricting ordinance and revert to previously established district lines. The writ was denied, and appellants argued that respondent failed to enact the initiative without change as required by Cal. Elec. Code § 3711 and was, therefore, required to submit it to voters, that respondent was precluded from adopting a redistricting ordinance with an effective date before the general election, and that a time limitation of 30 days to collect referendum petition signatures violated equal protection. The court affirmed and held that the purpose of § 3711 was to preserve the right of legislating by initiative on the county level but that the state chose to limit county voters to an indirect initiative. The court held that respondent made no changes in substantive law when it enacted the original ordinance. The court held that there was no violation in passing a redistricting ordinance with an effective date between the primary and general election, but with an operative date after the general election.


OUTCOME: Denial of appellant voters' application for a writ of mandate seeking order requiring respondent Board of Supervisors and Registrar of Voters of Alameda County to adopt an ordinance that would repeal a redistricting ordinance was affirmed because there was no violation in passing a redistricting ordinance with an effective date between the primary and general election but with an operative date after the general election.

 

860 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



In re Feiock


No. G003512


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Three


180 Cal. App. 3d 649; 225 Cal. Rptr. 748; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1536



April 30, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Real Party in Interest Wife for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied August 14, 1986. Lucas, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of contempt is annulled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner contemnor sought reversal of the order of the trial court (California), which held petitioner in contempt for his failure to pay child support. Petitioner challenged the mandatory presumption of contempt found in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1209.5.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered petitioner contemnor to pay child support as part of a dissolution action. Petitioner failed to make any payments for approximately five months. The state brought a contempt action. The trial court sustained the contempt allegations, applying the presumption that proof that a child support order was issued and proof that petitioner failed to comply was prima facie evidence of contempt of court, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1209.5. Petitioner sought reversal. The court annulled the judgment of contempt and held that the mandatory nature of the presumption in § 1209.5 unconstitutionally lessened the state's burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt the necessary element that petitioner had the ability to pay. The court found that noncompliance with the trial court's order did not compel the conclusion that petitioner had the ability to pay. The court held that the statute only authorized a permissive inference.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the judgment of contempt against petitioner contemnor for failure to pay child support. The court ruled that statutory mandatory presumption of contempt was unconstitutional.

 

861 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


McCall v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


No. H000864.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT.


189 Cal. App. 3d 532; 225 Cal. Rptr. 621; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1527; 51 Cal. Comp. Cases 201



April 29, 1986  
April 29, 1986


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE--SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review granted July 31, 1986 (S.F. 25041)
Review dismissed June 25, 1987 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 6th Dist.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion has been Reprinted for the Original Opinion of April 29, 1986, previously reported at 180 Cal. App. 3d 538.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee appealed the judgment of respondent Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (California), which held, after reconsideration, that respondent employer's right to a credit under Cal. Lab. Code § 3861, for compensation received by petitioner from a medical malpractice action settlement was not precluded by Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.1.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee received workers' compensation benefits for an injury sustained at work, and settled a separate medical malpractice action against the hospital that treated her. Respondent Workers' Compensation Appeals Board held that Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.1 did not override respondent employer's right to a credit under Cal. Lab. Code § 3861, against respondent employer's liability for workers' compensation benefits to the extent that petitioner received compensation in the malpractice settlement. On review sought by petitioner, the court affirmed. The court found that Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.1(a) allowed for the introduction of evidence of collateral source benefits in medical malpractice actions, and that Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.1(b) did not apply to preclude reimbursement to respondent. The court determined that by giving the words of the statute their ordinary and plain meaning, § 3333.1(b) only applied in the limited circumstance of a trial of the medical malpractice action. Because petitioner settled with the hospital before trial, the court held that respondent was entitled to a credit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Workers' Compensation Appeals Board, which held that respondent employer was not precluded from receiving a credit for compensation received by petitioner employee from a medical malpractice settlement. The court held that the statutory preclusion on recovery did not apply because there was no trial where evidence of collateral benefits was introduced.

 

862 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Armstrong


No. A028438.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


180 Cal. App. 3d 313; 225 Cal. Rptr. 545; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1509



April 25, 1986 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review denied August 14, 1986 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 6013, Jacqueline Taber, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which was entered on the jury finding that defendant was guilty of false imprisonment by violence or menace and of two counts of robbery and on the trial court's finding that defendant had suffered a prior conviction for robbery for which defendant served a prison term.


OVERVIEW: After a jury found defendant guilty of false imprisonment by violence or menace and of two counts of robbery, the trial court dismissed the jury. Thereafter a hearing was held, following which the trial court found that defendant had suffered a prior robbery conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, but remanded the case for a trial on the issue of the prior felony conviction because defendant did not waive his right of trial by jury, which was assured by Cal. Penal Code § 1025, Cal. Const. art. I, § 16, and the federal Constitution. The court held that where defendant matched the physical description given by a witness and defendant's fingerprints were found on stolen property, the victim's in-the-field identification of defendant was not so impermissibly suggestive as to give rise to a very substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification. The court ruled that the trial court did not err in admitting defendant's confession because the police officer's good faith confrontation did not render the confession involuntary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, holding that the victim's identification of defendant was not so impermissibly suggestive as to give rise to a substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification, and that defendant's confession was not coerced. The court remanded the case for a trial on the issue of the prior felony conviction because defendant had a right to trial by jury on that issue.

 

863 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Federal Savings & Loan Ins. Corp. v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 25304


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


180 Cal. App. 3d 336; 225 Cal. Rptr. 422; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1511



April 25, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Real Party in Interest for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied July 30, 1986.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ issue, directing the respondent court to dismiss the writ of attachment previously issued upon the request of American Savings and Loan, and to dismiss the underlying action brought by American against San Marino (San Joaquin County Superior Court No. 179526).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Federal Savings and Loan Insurance Corporation (FSLIC), as sole conservator for a bank under 12 U.S.C.S. § 1464(d)(6)(D), sought a peremptory writ of prohibition to restrain respondent Superior Court of San Joaquin County (California), from proceeding further on a complaint filed against the bank and to direct respondent to dismiss the action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: In a dispute over the assets of a bank in conservatorship, under 12 U.S.C.S. § 1464(d)(6)(D), with petitioner Federal Savings and Loan Insurance Corporation (FSLIC), petitioner sought a peremptory writ of prohibition to restrain respondent Superior Court of San Joaquin County (California) from proceeding further on a complaint filed against the bank and to direct respondent to dismiss the action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The court granted the writ of prohibition and held that respondent lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear the dispute. To ensure that all claims against a failed savings and loan association placed in receivership were expeditiously resolved in a single forum, Congress provided, in § 1464(d)(6)(C), that no court could restrain or affect the exercise of powers or functions of a conservator or receiver. Congress intended to give the FSLIC, acting as receiver of an insolvent association, exclusive authority to administratively resolve creditors' claims in order to facilitate speedy liquidation. Section 1464(d)(6)(C) set forth a jurisdictional prerequisite that the right to judicial review would vest only after completion of an administrative action.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner Federal Savings and Loan Insurance Corporation's application and issued a writ directing respondent trial court to dismiss the underlying action because respondent lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear the dispute until administrative remedies were exhausted.

 

864 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Vega-Hernandez


No. A028882


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


179 Cal. App. 3d 1084; 225 Cal. Rptr. 209; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1463



April 14, 1986 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Pursuant to rules 976 and 976.1, California Rules of Court, this opinion is certified for publication except for parts I, II, III and IV.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Mendocino County, No. 8151-C, Timothy W. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The restitution order is stricken and the cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with the views set forth herein to determine whether a restitution order is warranted under former Government Code section 13967. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Mendocino County (California) that convicted him of injuring two victims while driving under the influence of alcohol and in a hit and run with injury, in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23153(a), (b), and § 20001, sentenced him and ordered that restitution be paid to the victims for medical costs, property losses, and general damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his convictions for injuring two victims while driving under the influence of alcohol and in a hit and run with injury, in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23153(a), (b), § 20001. The trial court sentenced appellant and ordered that restitution be paid to the victims for medical costs, property losses, and general damages. On appeal, the court found that the trial court's restitution order exceeded its authority. Cal. Const. art. I, § 28(b) was not a self-executing constitutional provision and neither statutory nor constitutional authority supported the trial court's order of direct restitution. The order lacked statutory basis under either the presently effective or then-applicable framework, neither of which provided for direct restitution, orders greater than $ 10,000, or compensation for property losses or pain and suffering. The court remanded, requesting a more reliable factual basis to be developed for restitution, and that appellant be provided a reasonable opportunity to be heard to determine whether a restitution order was warranted under former Cal. Gov't Code § 13967. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of restitution and remanded for further proceedings because neither statutory nor constitutional authority supported the trial court's order of direct restitution. Otherwise, the court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of injuring two victims while driving under the influence of alcohol and in a hit and run with injury.

 

865 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Mohlmann v. City of Burbank


No. B015571


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


179 Cal. App. 3d 1037; 225 Cal. Rptr. 109; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1459



April 11, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Respondent City of Burbank for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied July 9, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 477605, Robert H. O'Brien, Judge, and John Zebrowski, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained respondent city and police officers' demurrer and dismissed appellant's complaint for false arrest.


OVERVIEW: After being arrested by respondent police officers, appellant arrestee brought a claim against respondents and the city for false arrest. At trial, respondents demurred to appellant's claim pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 911.2, which required that a claim for relief from a government entity be presented no later than the 100th day after the accrual of the cause of action. The court sustained respondents' demurrer and dismissed the claim, apparently on the grounds that § 945.3, as amended, barred appellant from bringing the claim. On review, the court reversed, holding that § 945.3, which prevented police and their employers from being sued for false arrest while criminal charges following an arrest were pending, did not require the plaintiff to file a claim within the applicable period under the California Tort Claims Act. The court ruled that § 945.3, as originally enacted and applicable at the time of appellant's claim, suspended the requirement to present notice of a claim until the underlying criminal proceedings were completed. The court also ruled that retroactivation of § 945.3, as amended, would be unconstitutional in that it would cut off appellant's remedy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of appellant arrestee's false arrest complaint against respondent city and police officers. The court ruled that appellant was not barred from bringing the complaint because at the time of the action the applicable statute of limitations was tolled. The court also refused to retroactivate the amended statute to bar appellant's complaint because such application would be unconstitutional.

 

866 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Winnett v. Roberts


Civ. No. 24354


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


179 Cal. App. 3d 909; 225 Cal. Rptr. 82; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1447



April 8, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 5, 1986, and Respondents' Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied June 25, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of El Dorado County, No. 42346, William E. Byrne and Charles F. Fogerty, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the cause remanded to the trial court with directions to declare the $ 7,000 note usurious. The court is also directed to order cancellation of the trustee's sale, the trustee's deed and the deed of trust, to quiet plaintiffs' title as against defendants, and to take such other action as the justice of the case requires.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff borrower challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California), which denied his motion to set aside a trustee's sale and trustee's deed. Plaintiff had brought an action to enjoin the foreclosure sale of real property under a trust deed securing a promissory note held by defendant lender.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff borrower contended that a note, which called for interest at an annual rate of 40 percent, was usurious. The court noted that the loan at issue was usurious unless the real estate broker exemption applied. The court found that the transaction was between plaintiff, a real estate broker, and defendant lender, each acting on his own behalf, and that there was no third party licensed real estate broker acting for compensation as intermediary. The court concluded that the loan was not "arranged" by a broker within the meaning of the usury law; therefore, the loan was not exempt from the proscription of Cal. Const. art. XV and was usurious. The court found that plaintiff tendered to defendant an amount in excess of his legal obligation, which was only the principal; therefore, he was released from all subsequent liability for interests, costs, and attorney fees incurred by defendant in connection with the foreclosure proceedings. The court reversed and found that plaintiff's payment in full of the underlying debt also discharged both the obligation and the deed of trust, so he was entitled to a full reconveyance of the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment is and remanded the cause to the trial court with directions to declare the note usurious. The court also directed the trial court to order cancellation of the trustee's sale, the trustee's deed, and the deed of trust, and to quiet plaintiff borrower's title as against defendant lender.

Singer Co. v. Superior Court


No. F006130


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


179 Cal. App. 3d 875; 225 Cal. Rptr. 159; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1445



April 7, 1986 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue directing respondent court: (1) to vacate its order of June 18, 1985, finding the settlement between Cool-Temp and plaintiffs in good faith and on that basis dismissing the first, second, fifth, and sixth causes of action in Singer's cross-complaint against Cool-Temp for partial indemnity, contribution, and declaratory relief as to personal injury claims and (2) to allow Singer further discovery as discussed herein before holding any further hearing to determine the good faith of Cool-Temp's settlement with plaintiffs. Singer shall recover from Cool-Temp its costs (not including attorney fees) incurred in petitioning this court for relief. ( Oksner v. Superior Court (1964) 229 Cal.App.2d 672 [40 Cal.Rptr. 621].)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner alleged tortfeasor sought a writ of mandate to vacate an order of respondent, Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which found that a settlement between real party in interest joint tortfeasor and the injured parties was in good faith and barred petitioner's cross-complaint.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner alleged tortfeasor contended that respondent, Superior Court of Fresno County, should have given it an opportunity to complete discovery against real party in interest joint tortfeasor before determining that real party in interest's settlement with the injured parties was in good faith. The court found that petitioner was named as a cross-defendant after real party in interest had settled with the injured parties. The court determined that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §§ 877 & 877.6 discharged real party in interest from further liability if the settlement was in good faith. Because petitioner was unnamed until after the settlement even though its potential liability had been known, the court concluded that petitioner had a due process right to challenge the good faith determination and a right to limited discovery. The court granted the writ of mandate to vacate the previous order and permit discovery before another hearing in which petitioner would have the burden of showing a lack of good faith.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandate to respondent, Superior Court of Fresno County, because petitioner alleged tortfeasor, who was unnamed despite potential liability, had a right to discovery and to challenge the determination that a settlement by real party in interest joint tortfeasor was in good faith.

Delucchi v. County of Santa Cruz


No. H000161


Court of Appeal of California, Sixth Appellate District


179 Cal. App. 3d 814; 225 Cal. Rptr. 43; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1438



April 3, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 30, 1986, and the Petition of Plaintiffs and Appellants for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied June 18, 1986. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1986. See 107 S.Ct. 46.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Cruz County, Nos. 83506 and 82382, Roland K. Hall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment below is affirmed insofar as it denies plaintiffs/cross-appellants' claims under The Civil Rights Act and requires a discretionary permit for the construction of additional dwellings on the subject property. In all other respects, the judgment is reversed and the trial court ordered to enter judgment in favor of appellants, the County and the Commission. The injunction issued by the trial court is dissolved. Each party is to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners, defendant county, and defendant commission sought review of an order of Superior Court, Santa Cruz County (California) that granted plaintiffs' request for injunctive relief, found plaintiffs were required to obtain permits before constructing additional structures, and denied plaintiffs' claims under the Civil Rights Act of 1871, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowners commenced two actions against defendant county and defendant commission, alleging the adoption of a revised zoning regulation constituted a breach of an agricultural preservation contract and violated plaintiff's constitutional rights in addition to their rights under the Civil Rights Act of 1871 (Act), 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court enjoined defendants from modifying the contract. The trial court also determined a discretionary permit was required for the construction of any additional dwellings, but not greenhouses, on the property. The trial court further ruled the Act, § 1983 was inapplicable. All parties sought review. On review, the court affirmed the denial of plaintiffs' claims under the Act, § 1983, and the part of the order requiring plaintiffs to apply for a permit, because plaintiffs had no cause of action under the Act, § 1983, and Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 30600 mandated permits. However, the court dissolved the injunction, reversed the remainder of the trial court's findings, and directed the entry of judgment for defendants because the contract did not prohibit defendant county from changing the zoning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the order that denied plaintiff landowners' civil rights claims and required a permit for the construction of additional dwellings, because no taking occurred and permits were mandated by statute. But the court dissolved the injunction, reversed the remainder of the order, and directed judgment for defendant county and defendant commission because the contract did not prohibit zoning changes.

Univ. Ford Chrysler-Plymouth,inc v. New Motor Vehicle Bd.


No. D001579


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


179 Cal. App. 3d 796; 224 Cal. Rptr. 908; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1436



April 3, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied April 24, 1986, and the Petitions of Appellants University Chrysler-Plymouth, Inc. and New Motor Vehicle Board for Review by the Supreme Court were Denied July 16, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, Nos. 512428, 512908, Jack R. Levitt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, new car dealership and New Motor Vehicle Board (board), sought review of an order from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which granted respondent car manufacturer's petition for writ of mandate and set aside board's decision as composition of board denied respondent its constitutionally guaranteed right to an impartial tribunal.


OVERVIEW: After respondent car manufacturer terminated its agreement with appellant new car dealer (dealer), dealer filed a protest of termination with appellant New Motor Vehicle Board (board). Board adopted the decision of the administrative law judge that respondent lacked good cause to terminate the dealership and the recommendation that the dealership continue, but relocate within two years. Both respondent and dealer filed petitions for writs of mandate to set aside the decision. The trial court granted respondent's petition, finding that board's composition which included new car dealers as members, but specifically excluded any car manufacturers as members, denied respondent's constitutional right to an impartial tribunal. Upon review, the court affirmed, finding that the provisions of Cal. Veh. Code §§ 3050(d) and 3066(d), which prevented new car dealer members of board from deciding matters involving dealer-manufacturer disputes, but permitted them to participate in, hear, comment, and advise other members, had the effect of denying a manufacturer litigant its constitutional right to an impartial tribunal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's writ of mandate setting aside appellant New Motor Vehicle Board's (board) decision, finding that the statutory provisions that permitted new car dealer members of board to participate in dealer-manufacturer disputes, but prevented them from actually rendering a decision, had the effect of depriving car manufacturer litigants their constitutional right to an impartial tribunal.

Mendez v. Community Hospital


No. B009295.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


179 Cal. App. 3d 705; 225 Cal. Rptr. 24; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1430



April 2, 1986 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review den. July 31, 1986 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NEC 25604, Robert B. Lopez, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which, after a jury trial, awarded plaintiff minor damages for medical and nursing care, lost future earnings, and pain and suffering, in a medical malpractice suit. Defendant sought an order reducing the noneconomic portion of the damages pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.2, and an amendment to the economic damages to be paid on a periodic basis.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff minor suffered permanent brain damage, leaving her substantially retarded, with a mental age of five months at 10 years of age. Plaintiff filed suit against defendant hospital, seeking damages for medical malpractice. The jury awarded plaintiff for medical, nursing care, lost future earnings, and pain and suffering. Defendant filed a motion seeking an order reducing the noneconomic portion (pain and suffering) of the judgment pursuant to Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.2, and an amendment to the judgment, applicable to economic loss damages, to be paid on a periodic basis pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. § 667.7. Defendant was denied and appealed. The court affirmed, reducing the noneconomic portion of the award by 92 percent. The court held that § 667.7 was applicable and remanded to the trial court to make a periodic payment order for the economic portion (lost earnings, medical, nursing, and training expenses) of the damages. The court, rejecting defendant's claim of excessive damages, held that there was credible evidence to support jury's award. The court held that the Cal. Health & Safety Code § 1768 was inapplicable and that plaintiff's expert witness was qualified to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for plaintiff minor, but reduced the noneconomic portion of the award by 92 percent. The court disagreed with defendant hospital's claim that damages awarded were excessive. The court remanded to the trial court with instructions to make an order for periodic payments for lost earnings, medical, nursing and training expenses, stating that interest accrued on the entire amount of unpaid judgment.

 

871 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Leo v. Superior Court


No. B017718


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


179 Cal. App. 3d 274; 225 Cal. Rptr. 15; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1395



March 27, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied June 20, 1986.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ is discharged and the peremptory writ of mandate is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a peremptory writ to review a decision by respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), denying its petition to prohibit people, the real party in interest, from changing its decision on seeking the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with three robberies and murder, committed during the robbery with a sawed off shotgun, which violated Cal. Pen. Code §§ 211, 187, 190.2(a)(17), 12022.5, and 1203.06(a)(1). The people, the real party in interest, (people) initially decided not to seek the death penalty, but changed its decision after reviewing new aggravating evidence. When respondent trial court denied petitioner's motion to prohibit a change in the death penalty decision, petitioner sought a peremptory writ, which the court denied for two reasons. First, there was no enforceable contract between the parties that barred a change, and petitioner did not give up valuable constitutional rights because he was entitled to a death penalty trial if needed. The court noted that petitioner was not denied due process of law because the trial had not begun and he had ample time to prepare a defense. Second, people's decision to pursue the death penalty was not arbitrary or cruel and or unusual punishment under the federal or state constitutions because the new evidence resulted in a material change in the circumstances, and people properly exercised prosecutorial discretion.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's peremptory writ to prohibit people, the real party in interest, (people) from changing its decision and seeking the death penalty. The court held that there was no enforceable contract between the parties that barred the change, petitioner did not give up valuable constitutional rights or was denied due process. The court ruled that the people's decision was not arbitrary and was within its discretion.

Save Oxnard Shores v. Cal. Coastal Com


No. B003988


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Six


179 Cal. App. 3d 140; 224 Cal. Rptr. 425; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 1382



March 26, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied April 23, 1986, and Respondent's Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied June 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. SP 50444, William L. Peck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment declaring the Commission's action invalid is reversed and the court is instructed to accept the returns to the alternative writ which were improperly stricken. The judgment in all other respects is affirmed because the Commission's action in compliance with the alternative writ rendered the SOS petition moot. Each party to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association and defendant commission challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California) which struck defendant's return vacating a conditional certification of a highly disputed land use plan permitting residential construction, in response to an alternative writ of mandamus issued by the trial court. Intervenor lot owners cross-challenged the denial of attorney fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: After defendant commission conditionally certified a land use plan, plaintiff association filed a petition for a peremptory writ. The trial court issued an alternative writ and intervenor lot owners then filed a complaint seeking to discharge the alternative writ and denial of the peremptory writ. Defendant then filed a return vacating its conditional certification and intervenors filed a motion to strike defendant's return. The trial court ruled that defendant's return was invalid, denied the peremptory writ, and dismissed plaintiff's petition, discharged the alternative writ, and awarded costs to intervenors. Plaintiff and defendant challenged the trial court's judgment and intervenors cross-challenged. The court reversed the trial court judgment and instructed acceptance of defendant's return because defendant's return was an appropriate response to the alternative writ issued by the trial court and intervenors were without standing to stay the alternative writ because they did not intervene until after the alternative writ was issued. The court affirmed the denial of attorney fees and costs to intervenors because they were not successful parties in the litigation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment striking defendant commission's return as invalid and instructed that defendant's return be accepted because defendant's return appropriately complied with the alternative writ of mandamus issued by the trial court. The court stated that intervenor landowners were unable to stay the alternative writ and the court affirmed the denial the judgment denying intervenors attorney fees and costs.

Nicolet, Inc. v. Superior Court


No. A030879, No. A030933, No. A030934.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


224 Cal. Rptr. 408; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2745



March 25, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review granted June 24, 1986 (S.F. 25027)
May 14, 1987 Dism. as moot and the request directing publication of the Ct. App. opn. was denied. Previously Reported at: 188 Cal. App. 3d 28.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner asbestos manufacturers sought writs of mandate reversing certain choice of law rulings made by respondent Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) in petitioners' actions against real party insurers.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner asbestos manufacturers filed actions against real party insurers alleging bad faith refusal to defend and indemnify claims and seeking punitive and compensatory damages. Respondent superior court ruled that Pennsylvania and English law applied to the questions of punitive damages. Petitioners argued that California law applied to the issue. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate commanding respondent to set aside those portions of its orders determining that Pennsylvania law and English law governed the actions on the question of punitive damages for bad faith conduct and to enter orders holding that California law applied. The court applied a "comparative impairment" approach, the court found that requiring California to adopt Pennsylvania's rule against punitive damages would create an archaic result in the context of the modern realities of the insurers' role as a multistate corporation and would require California to assist Pennsylvania in sheltering a corporation whose blatant misconduct, if proved, might cause damage outside its home state. The court also held that English law, which also did not allow punitive damages in this case, would not apply.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate commanding respondent superior court to set aside those portions of its order determining that Pennsylvania law and English law applied to petitioner asbestos manufacturers' action against real party insurers on the issue of punitive damages. The court ordered respondent to rule that California law applied to the issue of such damages.

 

874 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


O'Hare v. Superior Court


No. D003356.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


179 Cal. App. 3d 46; 224 Cal. Rptr. 765; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2748



March 25, 1986 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As modified Apr. 16, 1986; Review granted June 24, 1986 (L.A. 32209)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied his motion that venue be transferred to downtown branch. He then filed for a writ of mandate with the court which was denied. The state supreme court granted a petition for review of denial and on transfer, the court issued an alternative writ. Appellant contended that he was constitutionally entitled to a jury drawn from the entire county.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with numerous offenses including, kidnapping, under Cal. Penal Code § 207, and assault by means of force likely to produce great bodily injury, under Cal. Penal Code § 245(a)(1). Appellant sought to have his felony trial moved from the north part of the county to the downtown branch because the jury venire in the north county contained a significantly lower percentage of jury-eligible Black persons than the venire for the downtown branch. Appellant filed a petition with the court for a writ of mandate to have his case transferred. The petition was denied without prejudice. Appellant then filed a motion with the trial court to transfer venue to downtown, which was denied. Appellant then filed a second petition with the court, which was denied. The state supreme court granted his petition for review of the denial of his second petition and on transfer, the court issued an alternative writ. The court denied the writ, reasoning that while an accused had a right to a jury selected from a fair cross section of the community, there was no constitutional impediment to the designation of the north county as a "community" from which jurors were to be drawn.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of mandate directing the trial court to provide defendant with a jury panel drawn from the entire county was denied because defendant only had a right to a jury panel selected from a fair cross section of the community.

 

875 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Potter


No. F004298


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


179 Cal. App. 3d 73; 224 Cal. Rptr. 312; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2749



March 25, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied July 9, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kings County, No. 33277, Larry G. McKee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order appealed from is reversed and the cause is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Wife to have her costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of the order entered by the Superior Court of Kings County (California) which denied her motion to modify a dissolution judgment to divide respondent husband's military retirement benefits. The trial court declared Cal. Civ. Code § 5124 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The stipulated judgment of dissolution of the marriage of appellant wife and respondent husband confirmed respondent's military retirement benefits to him as his separate property, based on existing federal decisional law. The judgment became final before the effective date of the Federal Uniform Services Former Spouses' Protection Act (FUSFSPA), 10 U.S.C.S. § 1408. The trial court had not reserved jurisdiction of the case. Appellant moved to modify the dissolution judgment, based on Cal. Civ. Code § 5124, which permitted modification of community property judgments and agreements entered in the hiatus period between the federal decision and the enactment of FUSFSPA. The trial court denied the motion and declared § 5124 unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that § 5124 was constitutional because the impairment to existing contracts was sufficiently necessary to the public welfare to justify the impairment. The statute did not violate due process, nor the contract clause. Section 5124 did not attempt to override or expand on FUSFSPA. The clear intent and effect of § 5124 was to provide a procedure by which final community property settlements and judgments could be reopened.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court which denied appellant wife's petition to modify the judgment of dissolution to include division of respondent husband's military retirement benefits because the statute permitting the judgment to be reopened was not unconstitutional. Appellant was awarded costs on appeal.

 

876 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Rotary Club of Duarte v. Bd. of Dirs.


No. B001663


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


178 Cal. App. 3d 1035; 224 Cal. Rptr. 213; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2722



March 17, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 9, 1986, and Respondents' Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied June 18, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 244753, Max F. Deutz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. The matter is remanded to the trial court with directions to enter a new and different judgment in favor of Rotary Club of Duarte mandating the Board of Directors of Rotary International and Rotary District 530 to reinstate Rotary Club of Duarte's charter thereby reinstating it as a member of Rotary International and Rotary District 530 and permanently enjoining Rotary International and Rotary District 530 from enforcing or attempting to enforce its male-only-membership restriction against Rotary Club of Duarte.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a rotary club and two women, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that respondent, the International Rotary Club, could lawfully revoke appellant's charter and that respondent's male-only policy did not violate the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 51, or Cal. Const. art. I, § 8.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, two women and a local Rotary club, sought review of the lower court's decision that the male-only policy of respondent, the International Rotary Club, was not a violation of the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 51. The charter of appellant club was revoked after the club admitted the two individual appellants and a third woman. The trial court held that respondent and the individual local clubs were not business establishments within the meaning of the Unruh Act. The Unruh Act expressly prohibited sex based discrimination by business establishments. The lower court also found that to preclude enforcement of respondent's male-only policy in the state of California would effect the freedom of association of persons outside of the state. On review, the court found that respondent was clearly a business establishment that conferred considerable benefit on its members. The court also held that freedom of association, while a fundamental freedom, did not protect respondent from the effect of the Unruh Act. As such, the court reversed the lower court's decision denying appellants' injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed. The charter of appellant local rotary club was improperly revoked when appellant club admitted appellant women, because respondent International Rotary Club's male-only policy constituted sex discrimination under California law, and the rotary clubs constituted "business establishments."

Howard v. Santa Monica Rent Control Bd.


No. B013459.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


178 Cal. App. 3d 912; 223 Cal. Rptr. 899; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2711



March 14, 1986 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing April 11, 1986; Review Denied June 26, 1986 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. WEC 84189, Laurence J. Rittenband, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant rent control board appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted plaintiff landlords' petition for a writ of mandate, ordering defendant to set aside its decision and to recalculate plaintiffs' allowable rent increases.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landlords of apartment building subject to city rent control filed a petition with defendant rent control board for individual rent adjustment. Defendant granted increases for capital improvements, but determined that interest payments were excluded from consideration as operating expenses. The trial court entered judgment granting plaintiffs' petition for a writ of mandate, ordering defendant to set aside its decision and to take interest payments into account when recalculating plaintiffs' rent increases, and defendant appealed. The court held that, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1094.5, the trial court should have used the substantial evidence standard of review, rather than the independent judgment standard, but that the trial court did not need to reconsider defendant's decision because it could not have been supported by substantial evidence where material evidence regarding debt service was excluded. The court held that defendant was required to consider debt service as an operating expense, but that defendant was not obligated to guarantee plaintiffs' break-even point in order to meet the requirements of a fair return. The court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter to defendant rent control board because defendant was required to consider debt service as an operating expense in making decision on plaintiff landlords' petition for rent adjustment.

Riley v. Fitzgerald


No. B008127


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Six


178 Cal. App. 3d 871; 223 Cal. Rptr. 889; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2707



March 13, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 9, 1986. Gilbert, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted. Appellants' Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied July 10, 1986. Bird, C. J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County, No. 58161, Warren C. Conklin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Therefore, we hold that, presented with the issue before us, Texas courts would find article 7.12 a bar to Rileys' claims. The judgments appealed from are affirmed. Each party to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, sole shareholders, sought review of the order from the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County (California), which held that appellants' claim against respondent companies was barred by Tex. Bus. Corp. Act Ann. art. 7.12 time limitations, in an action brought by appellants against respondents asserting injuries to and fraud upon appellants' dissolved corporation.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, sole shareholders, dissolved their Texas corporation and assigned its assets to themselves. Appellants filed suit against respondent companies, for breach of fiduciary duty, restraint of sale or transfer of royalty rights, constructive trust and accounting, based on a joint venture involving oil leases. The trial court held that appellants had not brought the claim within the grace period of Tex. Bus. Corp. Act Ann. art. 7.12. On appeal, appellants contended that California law should apply, rules involving dissolving corporations were irrelevant, and current Texas law precluded the result. The court held that appellants waived the issue of applicable California law as they raised the claim for the first time on appeal, and that, even if the issue was not waived, the trial court was correct in applying art. 7.12, as Texas had a greater interest. The court held that equitable estoppel was not available, as art. 7.12 was not a statute of limitations, and that appellants were afforded no more rights under the statute than a defunct corporation. The court held that appellants subjected themselves to Texas law and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that held that appellants, sole shareholders', claim against respondent companies was barred. The court held that as Texas had a greater interest in the case, Texas law should have been applied, and appellants' claim was barred as it failed to fall within the grace period of the Texas statute, and that equitable estoppel did not apply as the statute was not a statute of limitations.

Moore v. Preventive Medicine Medical Group, Inc.


No. B009312


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Seven


178 Cal. App. 3d 728; 223 Cal. Rptr. 859; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2693



March 11, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 8, 1986, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. 59642, Sara Kleban Radin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reduced by $ 18,000 -- the amount the jury awarded Moore for the future loss of earnings in the real estate field. PMMG is also given credit for the amount of Dr. Mason's settlement ($ 5,000). In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed. Respondent to recover costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical group sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) after it rendered a decision against it in a medical malpractice case. Appellant argued that the judgment should be reversed because the lower court committed several errors in instructing the jury and the jury committed several acts of misconduct that deprived appellant of a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: Respondent patient was an actor and real estate salesman. During a physical examination, respondent told his doctor about a spot he had noticed on his ear lobe. Another doctor told respondent the mole was malignant melanoma. Respondent subsequently had part of his ear removed, along with the glands and lymph nodes. After surgery, an analysis of the removed tissues showed no evidence of any melanoma. In the medical malpractice case that followed, the lower court awarded judgment in favor of respondent. Appellant medical group argued that the judgment should be reversed because the lower court committed several errors in instructing the jury and the jury committed several acts of misconduct that deprived appellant of a fair trial. The lower court judgment was affirmed, as modified. The court reduced the judgment by $ 18,000, which was the amount the jury awarded respondent for the future loss of earnings in the real estate field. Appellant was also given credit for the amount of the physician's settlement ($ 5,000).


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment was affirmed as modified. The court reduced the judgment by $ 18,000, which was the amount the jury awarded respondent patient for the future loss of earnings in the real estate field. Appellant medical group was also given credit for the amount of the physician's settlement ($ 5,000).

In re Valenti


No. B016161


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Six


178 Cal. App. 3d 470; 224 Cal. Rptr. 10; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2671



March 5, 1986 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part I.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petitioner's Application for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied June 5, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. 88347, Steven Z. Perren, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of habeas corpus is denied and the order to show cause is discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus alleging the three and one-half year sentence for his convictions of five misdemeanors and imposition of additional time for violation of probation violated his equal protection rights as they were disproportionate, irregular, and consequently unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to consecutive sentences after he was convicted of five misdemeanors and given additional time for probation violation. Appellant filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus alleging that the consecutive sentences violated his equal protection rights, as they were disproportionate, irregular, and consequently unconstitutional. Appellant alleged that he had the right to have each sentence for each consecutive charge conform to limitations specified in Cal. Penal Code § 1170 for sentences on consecutive felonies. The court denied appellant's petition for habeas corpus finding that there was a significant difference between in the quality and duration of punishment, as well as in resultant long-term effects, which were brought about by a felony conviction as opposed to a misdemeanor conviction. Therefore, the distinctions in the sentencing for felonies and misdemeanors were justified and that distinctions created by the law were necessary to further governmental purpose.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus because his consecutive sentences for misdemeanor convictions was constitutional and did not violate his equal protection rights. The court found that appellant did not have the right to have the sentence for each consecutive charge conform to the limitations specified in the Penal Code for sentences on consecutive felonies.

Williams v. Superior Court


No. B016942.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


186 Cal. App. 3d 1373; 223 Cal. Rptr. 700; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2662



March 4, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review granted June 20, 1986 (L.A. 32206)
February 4, 1987 Trans to Ct. App., 2d Dist., Div. 7, for reconsideration in light of O'Hare v. Superior Court (1987) 43 Cal. 3d 86. (See 193 Cal. App. 3d 726)
Transferred by Williams v. Superior Court of County of Los Angeles, 234 Cal. Rptr. 778, 732 P.2d 1072, 1987 Cal. LEXIS 486 (Cal., Feb. 24, 1987)
Supplemental opinion at Williams v. Superior Court, 193 Cal. App. 3d 726, 238 Cal. Rptr. 488, 1987 Cal. App. LEXIS 1931 (Cal. App. 2d Dist., July 14, 1987)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by In re Williams, 2014 Cal. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2528 (Cal. App. 2d Dist., Apr. 9, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion has been Reprinted for the Original Opinion of March 4, 1986, previously reported at 178 Cal. App. 3d 360.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the West Judicial District of Los Angeles Superior Court (California), by way of petition for writ of prohibition and mandate because the court denied his motion to quash the jury venire for his first degree murder trial pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 187.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought a writ of mandate directing the trial court to vacate its denial of motion to quash venire. Defendant claimed blacks were underrepresented in his jury venire. The court concluded that the population of the "area served by the court" of which the jury venire must be fairly representative meant the population of the area within a 20-mile radius of each of the branch courts of the Los Angeles County Superior Court. The court concluded that defendant did not present statistics showing the percentage of juror-eligible blacks within a 20-mile radius of the courthouse to show fair-cross-section requirement violation in the jury venire; therefore, no prima facie showing of underrepresentation was made. The court held that because defendant did not have benefit of the court's definition of community, he should not be foreclosed from renewing his motion and making the relevant statistical showing of juror eligible blacks residing within the 20-mile radius of the Santa Monica courthouse. Moreover, because of the difficulty in obtaining such statistical data, the trial court should order such data provided to defendant and the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition and held that the trial court properly found defendant had not made the required prima facie showing of systematic underrepresentation. The court concluded that his motion was made without benefit of the court's definition of community; therefore, defendant should be allowed to renew his motion and make the relevant statistical showing of juror-eligible blacks residing within the 20-mile radius.

Palmer v. City of Ojai


Nos. B003987, B005635


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


178 Cal. App. 3d 280; 223 Cal. Rptr. 542; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2655



March 3, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 1, 1986, and the Opinion was Modified to Read as Printed Above. Respondents' Petition for Review by the Supreme Court was Denied June 20, 1986. Bird, C. J., and Reynoso, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, Nos. SP 51133 and 81161, William L. Peck and Joe D. Hadden, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment denying the petition for writ of mandate is reversed. The judgment dismissing the complaint for damages is affirmed. Each party to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land developer sought review of decisions by the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which denied both a petition for a writ and money damages. The two actions against respondent city were consolidated on appeal. In one, appellant sought a writ to compel respondent to issue a building permit and the second involved money damages for refusal to take action on permit applications.


OVERVIEW: Appellant land developer filed applications for permits to develop 31 acres of land. Two years later, no final decisions had been made on the applications. Cal. Res. Code §§ 21100.2, 21151.5, had one-year limitations, and respondent city did not meet the statutorily imposed time limits. Appellant sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent to do certain actions including the issuance of the permits. Appellant also filed an action for monetary damages caused by the delay in making a decision on the applications. The trial court granted respondent judgment on the pleadings in both actions. The trial court concluded that the statutory scheme created a mandatory duty to act within time limitations and the petition for a writ should have been granted. On review, the court concluded that there was a strong public policy that insulated land use planning from civil liability. The court reversed the judgment denying the petition for a writ of mandate. The judgment dismissing the complaint for damages was affirmed and each party was to bear its own costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the petition for a writ of mandate was reversed because the time limits created a mandatory duty on the part of respondent city to issue the permits. The judgment dismissing the complaint for money damages was affirmed because public policy insulated land use planning from civil liability.

 

883 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Cox


No. G000326.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


178 Cal. App. 3d 240; 223 Cal. Rptr. 655; 1986 Cal. App. LEXIS 2652



February 28, 1986 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review den. May 22, 1986 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. D-207055, J. Edgar Thompson Rutter II and Ronald Eugene Owen, Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which denied her motions to set aside a portion of an interlocutory decree that had awarded respondent ex-husband's retirement pension to him as separate property, in order that part of it be awarded to her as community property under the Federal Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act or Cal. Civ. Code § 5124.


OVERVIEW: Appellant ex-wife and respondent ex-husband were divorced and respondent was awarded his nondisability retirement pension as his separate property. Appellant filed a motion to set aside the full pension award to respondent in order that part thereof be awarded to her as community property. Appellant contended that the newly enacted Federal Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act (Act) was to be applied retroactively to final judgments. The lower court denied appellant's motion so she filed a similar motion under newly enacted Cal. Civ. Code § 5124, which was also denied. The court affirmed and held that the express language of the Act indicated that Congress had not intended it to be applied retroactively to final judgments made prior to its effective date and pursuant to a Supreme Court decision which declared that a pension belonged exclusively to a military spouse. The court found that because the Supreme Court decision was the supreme law of the land for nondisability military pension awards finalized between June 26, 1981 and February 1, 1983, § 5124 had to yield to such decision under the Supremacy Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, cl. 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of appellant ex-wife's motions to set aside a decree that awarded the respondent ex-husband's retirement pension to him, so that part of it be awarded to her as community property. The court held that Congress had not intended retroactive application of the Federal Uniformed Services Former Spouses' Protection Act to judgments that were final before its effective date.
