Volkswagen of Am. v. New Motor Vehicle Bd.


No. A012279


California Court of Appeal, First Appellate District, Division Four.


1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2387



July 18, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] CERTIFIED FOR PUBLICATION August 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: 1 Civ. 54039, Super. Ct. No. 78060.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant automobile manufacturer challenged the decision of the superior court (California), which denied its petition for a writ of mandamus. The manufacturer asserted that appellee Department of Motor Vehicles, New Motor Vehicle Board had abused its discretion when it ordered the manufacturer to consent to the transfer of a car dealership.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer disapproved of the transfer of a car dealership. The real parties in interest, transferee and dealership, petitioned the board, alleging that the decision was unreasonable. The board adopted the findings of an administrative law judge, which held that the withdrawal of consent to the transferee was unreasonable and ordered the manufacturer not to withhold its consent. The manufacturer sought a writ of mandamus, which the trial court denied. The court reversed. The court found that the statutory scheme of the California Automobile Franchise Act (Act), Cal. Veh. Code § 3000 et seq., failed to meet the criterion of due process that a tribunal must be impartial and not appear to have the likelihood or appearance of bias because the Act mandated the presence of car dealers on the board without any representation by the manufacturers. The court held that the manufacturer was entitled to raise the constitutional issue for the first time on appeal because it involved a pure question of law presented by undisputed facts, it fundamentally affected the validity of the judgment, and it entailed important public policy questions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court which denied the manufacturer's petition for a writ of mandamus seeking relief from a decision of the board, which found that the manufacturer's decision to disapprove of the transfer of a car dealership was unreasonable. The court remanded the case for further proceedings before a board acting without the participation of new motor vehicle dealer members.

 

974 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Schmidt v. Superior Court


No. B008475.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


185 Cal. App. 3d 31; 215 Cal. Rptr. 840; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2213



July 16, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] See 43 Cal. 3d 1060 for Supreme Court Opinion. Withdrawn from Bound Volume.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion Previously Reported at: 170 Cal. App. 3d 84.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mobile home buyers sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent Superior Court of Santa Barbara County to rehear their motion for summary judgment in their suit for declaratory and injunctive relief against the real parties in interest, mobile home park proprietors. Petitioners claimed that a park residency restriction for anyone under age 25 violated the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 51 et seq.


OVERVIEW: When petitioner mobile home buyers attempted to obtain a mobile home in a park operated by the real parties in interest, mobile home proprietors, petitioners were informed that their application had been rejected because of a policy not to allow anyone under the age of 25 to reside there. Petitioners brought suit and moved for summary judgment. Respondent trial court denied the motion, as a matter of law, on the grounds that Cal. Civ. Code § 798.76 carved out an exception to the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 51, by permitting mobile home parks to exclude families with children. Petitioners request a writ of mandate. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate that commanded respondent to rehear petitioners' motion for summary judgment. The court determined that it was unable to infer from § 798.76 any intent on the part of the legislature to interfere with its longstanding goal of increasing affordable housing for the general population. Instead § 798.76 carved out an exclusive right to draft age restrictions in a "senior" facility only. The policy of the real parties in interest was found to be arbitrary and in violation of the Unruh Civil Rights Act.


OUTCOME: A peremptory writ of mandate was issued that commanded respondent trial court to rehear petitioner mobile home buyers' motion for summary judgment filed against real parties in interest, mobile home park proprietors. The court concluded that state law allowed mobile home parks to exclude children only where the facilities were reserved for senior citizens. The age restrictions imposed against petitioners violated the Unruh Civil Rights Act.

 

975 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Pressler v. Irvine Drugs


No. G000381


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Three


169 Cal. App. 3d 1244; 215 Cal. Rptr. 807; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2206



July 12, 1985 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976(b), parts I, II, III, IV and V are not published as they do not meet the standards for publication.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The petition of plaintiff and appellant for review by the Supreme Court was denied September 24, 1985. Bird, C. J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 334134, James Randal Ross, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Each party to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties appealed decision from the Superior Court of Orange County, (California) in favor of plaintiff, diabetic, in an action for pharmaceutical malpractice and negligence. Following trial, the jury returned special verdict, finding liability on part of defendant, drug store. The court then asked the jury to break down lump sum award under special interrogatories. Then the court reduced the general damages under Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, drug store, appealed decision in favor of plaintiff, diabetic, in an action for pharmaceutical malpractice and negligence. Following trial, the jury returned special verdict, finding no negligence on the part of plaintiff and assigned liability to defendant. The court then asked the jury to break down the lump sum award pursuant to supplemental special interrogatories. Thereafter, the court reduced the general damages amount under Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.2, which placed a ceiling on noneconomic losses recoverable in an action for injury against a health care provider for professional negligence. Defendant appealed. Plaintiff cross-appealed, arguing was improper, once the jury had returned its verdict, to require a breakdown of lump sum award. On appeal, the court held although the proper procedure would have been to submit the interrogatories with the original verdict, under the circumstances the judgment was affirmed. Given uncertainty of Cal. Civ. Code § 3333.2's constitutionality at time of trial, thorough discussion of the issue among the court and both attorneys, and fact that mandatory requirements of the section were complied with, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in appeal by both parties from decision for plaintiff, diabetic, in an action for pharmaceutical malpractice and negligence. The court concluded that it was proper, once the jury had returned its verdict, for the court to require a breakdown in the lump sum award.

 

976 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Davis v. Superior Court


No. G002272


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Three


169 Cal. App. 3d 1054; 215 Cal. Rptr. 721; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2188



July 8, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Let a peremptory writ issue directing respondent court to vacate that section of its order of December 17, 1984, addressed to the second cause of action, and to enter an order denying the city's motion for order determining issues to be without substantial controversy on that cause of action. The alternative writ is discharged. 10



10 At oral argument, counsel for the city stated the third cause of action had been abandoned. To the extent the petition addresses this cause of action, the request for relief is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens sought review of the dismissal of their action against real parties in interest, the city by the Superior Court of Orange County, (California) in petitioners' action challenging the validity of the city's housing element.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner citizens challenged the validity of real party in interest, city's, housing element, alleging that it failed to adequately address and provide for low and moderate income housing. After the complaint was filed, the city revised the element and thereafter, the court granted city's motion to dismiss parts of petitioner's complaint. Petitioners contend that their complaint was still viable to the extent the new enactments do not answer their original objections, the city insists the complaint was premature or moot. The court granted a peremptory writ directing the lower court to vacate its dismissal of parts of petitioner's complaint and to enter an order denying the city's motion to dismiss. The court held that the complaint was not premature; it challenged the 1974 housing element which was then in existence, it does not suddenly become premature because new and different elements are later enacted. The court further held that the enactment of subsequent legislation does not automatically render a matter moot, that this issue may only be determined by addressing the original claims in relation to the latest enactment at a full adversarial hearing.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ directing respondent court to vacate that section of its order dismissing portions of petitioner's complaint, and to enter an order denying the city's motion for order determining issues to be without substantial controversy on that cause of action.

 

977 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bynum


No. AO21650.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


184 Cal. App. 3d 1267; 215 Cal. Rptr. 639; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2345



July 5, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review granted Oct. 17, 1985 (Crim. 24896)
Oct. 2, 1986 Trans. to Ct. App., 1st Dist., Div. 4, for reconsideration in light of People v. Collins (1986) 42 Cal. 3d 378.
Opn. filed January 6, 1987 not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 26852, Patricia Herron, Judge.

This Opinion has been Reprinted for the Original Opinion of July 5, 1985, previously reported at 169 Cal. App. 3d 992.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California) that convicted him of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of an armed robbery in which he intentionally inflicted great bodily injury upon the victim. The court found that the trial court had erred in granting the prosecution's motion to discover defense materials because the statute that allowed the discovery, Cal. Penal Code § 1102.5, violated defendant's right against self-incrimination. However, defendant could not complain on appeal of the state's reference to the materials because he had not made a timely objection at trial. Although a recent amendment to Cal. Const. that allowed unlimited use of prior felony convictions for impeachment purposes had not gone into effect at the time defendant committed the charged crimes, the trial court's error in this regard was harmless because the other evidence of guilt was strong. Therefore, the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the evidence of his guilt was strong enough that any error in admitting evidence of prior convictions for impeachment purposes was harmless, and because defendant had not made a timely objection at trial to the unconstitutional admission of defense materials.

 

978 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Richerson


No. B007172


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Six


169 Cal. App. 3d 1006; 215 Cal. Rptr. 706; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2346



July 5, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Barbara County, No. SM 41619, Zel Canter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California) that convicted him for the crime of grand theft as a result of the sale of mortgaged personal property with intent to defraud the mortgagee in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 538.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of violating Cal. Penal Code § 538, which prohibited the sale of property permitted to be mortgaged by Cal. Civ. Code § 2955 (repealed). The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. In so ruling, the court rejected appellant's argument that § 538 was unconstitutionally vague because § 2955 was repealed prior to the commission of his crime. The court observed that the repeal of § 2955 coincided with the enactment of Cal. Com. Code § 9602, which set forth the same definitions of property to be mortgaged as those previously relied on in § 2955. Noting that the repeal and enactment merely transferred the definition of mortgaged property, the court held that the information relating to possible mortgaged property was always available, and fair warning, as required by U.S. Const. amend. XIV, was provided. Moreover, the court observed that when a statute adopts a provision of another statute, the repeal of that other statute does not affect the adopting statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted appellant for the crime of grand theft as a result of the sale of mortgaged personal property with intent to defraud because the statute under which appellant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague because what types of personal property could be mortgaged had always been in the statutes and were easily discoverable.

 

979 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Gaenslen v. Bd. of Dirs.


No. A016711


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


185 Cal. App. 3d 563; 232 Cal. Rptr. 239; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1490



June 28, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 782459, J. Anthony Kline, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondent Hospital Board of Directors to reinstate his membership on hospital's medical staff. In this action, appellant was expelled from staff membership and his clinical privileges were terminated at the hospital, following an internal investigation and review process.


OVERVIEW: After an extensive investigation and review process by respondent Hospital Board of Directors, appellant doctor was expelled from staff membership and his clinical privileges were terminated at the hospital. Appellant petitioned the trial court for a writ of mandate pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1094.5(d) seeking to have his staff membership at the hospital restored. The trial court denied appellant's petition, and appellant challenged the trial court's judgment. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that appellant was not denied his right to fair procedure during the expulsion process because the hospital bylaws adequately articulated the standards of care, that the hospital was not required to give appellant notice of his deficient conduct as a prerequisite to expulsion, and appellant never objected to the composition of the judicial review committee. The court also found that the record was replete with substantial evidence to support appellant's expulsion. Finally, the court rejected appellant's argument that §1094.5(d) unconstitutionally denied him of his right to due process and equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant doctor's petition for a writ of mandate to reinstate his hosptial privleges. Appellant's rights to fair procedure were not violated, the review standards utilized by respondent Hospital Board of Directors were well defined and fair, and there was substantial evidence to support appellant's expulsion. The court also rejected appellant's claims that the procedural statute was unconstitutional.

 

980 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Brown


Crim. No. 40539


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


169 Cal. App. 3d 728; 215 Cal. Rptr. 465; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2317



June 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied September 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A020840, Pat Mullendore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The findings of special circumstances pursuant to Penal Code section 190.2, subdivision (a)(3) (multiple murders), as to counts II and XI, are reversed. The findings of special circumstances as to count II, pursuant to Penal Code section 190.2, subdivision (a)(17) (robbery and burglary), are reversed. The cause is remanded for further proceedings and for resentencing on counts VIII, XI, XIII, and XIV (rape and oral copulation) pursuant to Penal Code section 1170.1. In all other respects, including the findings of special circumstances as to count XI, pursuant to Penal Code section 190.2, subdivision (a)(17) (rape and burglary), the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) which convicted him of murder, rape, forcible oral copulation, kidnapping, robbery and found true special circumstances allegations as to murder, that a firearm was used in committing the offenses, that multiple murders were committed, and that defendant had not been free of custody for five years at the time the felonies were committed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, rape, forcible oral copulation, kidnapping, and robbery. Special circumstances allegations were found true as to the murder, that a firearm was used in committing the offenses, that multiple murders were committed, and that defendant had not been free of custody for five years at the time the felonies were committed. Defendant alleged that the jury was not representative and that findings as to the felony-murder rule and the special circumstances were improper without intent. The court affirmed, holding that because defendant did not object to jury selection at trial, he could not raise the issue on appeal. The special circumstances findings were proper as to one of the victims, despite the trial court's failure to instruct on intent, because the jury's verdict necessarily required a finding that the killing was intentional. However, as to the other victim, because the jury could have found true the special circumstances, without finding intent, the special circumstances as to that victim was reversed. The trial court also erred in not using the sentencing statute in effect when the crimes were committed. The case was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, rape, forcible oral copulation, kidnapping, and robbery because the felony murder rule was properly applied and defendant was precluded from raising an objection as to jury selection for the first time on appeal. The special circumstances findings as to one of the victims was reversed because the jury was not instructed as to the required intent for the special circumstances allegations.

 

981 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Talamantez


Crim. No. 15331


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


169 Cal. App. 3d 443; 215 Cal. Rptr. 542; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2292



June 19, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied July 5, 1985, and appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied September 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CRN 6506, Don Martinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Superior Court of San Diego County, California that convicted him of murder in the first degree based upon a finding of torture murder. The special circumstances of murder by torture, killing because of race and killing during the commission or attempted commission of a kidnapping, were found to be true. Defendant was sentenced to life without the possibility of parole plus two years for prior convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for murder in the first degree based upon a finding of torture murder and special circumstances of murder by torture, killing because of race and killing during the commission or attempted commission of a kidnapping, charging multiple errors. The court affirmed defendant's conviction on the basis that the jury was fully and properly instructed on the elements of murder, as well as the elements of murder by torture, and that there was no error in the court's instruction relating to aiding and abetting. The court held that defendant placed his specific intent in issue by putting forward a diminished capacity defense in relation to the special circumstances charge for torture murder, and that nothing in the factual record hinted at a lack of intent on defendant's part to torture the victim as he expressed his intent to put him to death. The court found that if a wrong instruction had been given, it was nonprejudicial as, beyond a reasonable doubt, had the jury been correctly instructed, it would not have reached a more favorable result based on the facts that defendant violently beat and tortured the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that the jury had been properly instructed on the elements of murder and murder by torture, and that there had been no prejudicial error in the trial court's failure to instruct the jury that aiding and abetting required that a defendant intentionally aid and abet the crime, as jury, if it had been correctly instructed, would not have reached a more favorable result based on evidence of record.

 

982 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Am. Olean Tile Co. v. Schultze


No. AO25640


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Five


169 Cal. App. 3d 359; 215 Cal. Rptr. 184; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2005



June 18, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. 256791, John J. Bible, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tile company sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) which found that the community property held by appellee wife was not liable for debts incurred by appellee husband after separation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant tile company filed a lawsuit against appellees, husband and wife, for nonpayment of a promissory note executed by appellee husband after the marriage was dissolved. Pursuant to the marital settlement agreement appellee husband received a community business as his separate property. Appellee wife received other property. Appellee husband signed a promissory note in favor of appellant for $ 13,747.80 for unpaid invoices that were merged into the promissory note. Appellee husband failed to make any payments on the note. Appellant file an amended complaint claiming former community property held by appellee wife was liable for the unpaid account and the promissory note since both were incurred and executed during her marriage to appellee husband. Appellant was granted a prejudgment attachment of a promissory note, secured by a deed of trust on real property, which was originally payable to appellees. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that appellee husband was dealing with the obligations of his separate property and not community property when he executed the promissory note to plaintiff. The pre-judgment attachment as to appellee wife was discharged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in ruling against appellant tile company as against appellee wife. Appellee husband was dealing with the obligations of his separate property and not community property when he executed the promissory note to plaintiff. Appellant's pre-judgment attachment as to appellee wife was discharged.

 

983 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Bourke v. East Bay Regional Park Dist.


No. AO14863.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


169 Cal. App. 3d 169; 215 Cal. Rptr. 312; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1986



June 12, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rev. den. Sept. 19, 1985, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 467617-5, Robert H. Kroninger and Donald P. McCullum, Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which dismissed her action against defendants, state transportation department and park district, under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 583.320, because it was not brought to a new trial within three years after issuance of a remittitur. Plaintiff asserted that the five-year provision of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 583.310, applied.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer brought a taxpayer's suit to set aside a sale of land between defendants, state transportation department and park district. Defendants successfully demurred, but the action was reversed and returned to the trial court after an appeal. Following plaintiff's continuance of a scheduled trial and removal from the civil active list, the action was dismissed because it was not brought to trial within three years after issuance of a remittitur. The court affirmed. The court held that dismissal of the action was mandatory under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 583.320, because a new trial had not been brought within three years. The court rejected plaintiff's assertion that the five-year provision of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 583.310, applied. The court held that this section only applied when there had been no trial. The court further held that plaintiff's hearing after the demurrer constituted a trial when the ruling resulted in a judgment of dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, and held that the trial court properly dismissed plaintiff taxpayer's action against defendants, state transportation department and park district, because it had not been brought to a new trial within three years. The court further held that the five-year statutory provision only applied when there was no trial.

 

984 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Berentsen


No. 22669.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD Dist.


171 Cal. App. 3d 137; 215 Cal. Rptr. 299; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2395



June 11, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, the Reporter of Decisions is directed to publish the Introduction, Facts, Discussion, I, A., Disposition, and the concurring opinion and not publish Discussion, I, B., II, III, IV and V.


Rev. granted Aug. 22, 1985 (S.F. 24918)
Aug. 1, 1986, App. dism. pursuant to stipulation.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Placer County, No. 54904, J. Richard Couzens, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband and appellant wife sought review of the final judgment of dissolution from the Superior Court of Placer County (California), which characterized appellants' residence as community property and denied appellant wife separate property contributions to the residence.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, husband and wife, challenged the lower court's final judgment of dissolution. Before marriage, appellants signed a written agreement that wife's inheritance was her separate property, and the couple improved their residence with funds from wife's inheritance. The trial court found that the residence was community property and denied appellant wife a separate property interest in it. The court reversed and remanded on the issue of appellant wife's reimbursement. The court applied Cal. Civ. Code § 4800.2 retroactively and concluded that appellant wife was entitled to reimbursement for separate property contributions to the acquisition of the residence unless she waived it in writing. Retroactive application of § 4800.2 did not violate appellant husband's rights under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or Cal. Const. art. I, § 16, because appellant husband's marital rights were not contractual obligations. Further, the court found that the state could exercise its police power to divest appellant husband of a vested right in the family residence. The court found that the trial court's characterization of the residence as community property was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's characterization of the family residence as community property and appellant husband's interest in it, but reversed and remanded as to appellant wife's reimbursement for her separate property contributions. The court retroactively applied a newly enacted statute to conclude that appellant wife was entitled to reimbursement for separate property contributions to the acquisition of the residence.

 

985 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Bell Cmty. Redevelopment Agency v. Woosley


Civ. Nos. B003190, B003007


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


169 Cal. App. 3d 24; 214 Cal. Rptr. 788; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 1974



June 7, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. 470402, Bruce R. Geernaert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The denial of the petition for writ of mandate is reversed. Let the writ issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant redevelopment agency challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied appellant's petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondent agency secretary to publish a notice that invited bids for a proposed $ 3 million tax allocation bond issue because the appropriation was allegedly in excess of that permitted under Cal. Const. art. XIII B.


OVERVIEW: Appellant redevelopment agency adopted a plan for an industrial redevelopment project. The project involved a $ 3 million tax allocation bond issue to effectuate the purchase of the property and the development. The bonds were to be repaid solely from tax increment funds. Respondent agency secretary refused to publish the notice that invited bids because the debt service on the bond issue allegedly constituted an appropriation in excess of that allowed under Cal. Const. art. XIII B. The trial court denied appellant's petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondent to publish the notice. Appellant sought review. The court reversed the trial court. The court held that Cal. Health & Safety Code § 33678 exempted tax increment financing from the requirements of art. XIII B. Under § 33678, the allocation and payment to redevelopment agencies of tax increments was not deemed to be a receipt of proceeds of taxes by the agency and was not subject to the appropriation limitations imposed by art. XIII B. The county was not levying and collecting taxes for appellant. The provisions of § 33678 were a valid legislative reconciliation of art. XIII B and the redevelopment law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and let the writ of mandate issue to compel respondent agency secretary to publish a notice that invited bids for a proposed $ 3 million tax allocation bond issue by appellant redevelopment agency because the constitutional limitations on appropriations did not apply to the allocation and payment to appellant of tax increments.

 

986 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Michael G.


Civ. No. F005001.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH Dist.


193 Cal. App. 3d 75; 214 Cal. Rptr. 755; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2181



June 6, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review granted Aug. 22, 1985 (See 44 Cal. 3d 283)


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion has been Reprinted for the Original Opinion of June 6, 1985, previously reported at 168 Cal. App. 3d 1188 and Reprinted at 184 Cal. App. 3d 774.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner ward of the court applied for a writ of habeas corpus and challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Fresno County (California), which ordered him confined in a secure facility during non-school hours for his contemptuous disobedience of a lawful court order that he attend school.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile court imposed a 48-hour period of confinement in secure facility for petitioner ward of the court's contemptuous disobedience of a lawful court order that he attend school. The juvenile court stayed the enforcement of the order to allow petitioner an opportunity for appellate review. Petitioner then applied for a writ of habeas corpus and claimed that a minor adjudged a ward of the juvenile court as a status offender under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 601(b) could not be punished for contempt by confinement in a secure facility during non-school hours. The court denied the writ and vacated the previously ordered stay. When Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 601(b) and 207(b) were read as a whole, it was clear that the legislature did not intend to eliminate or restrict the inherent powers of the juvenile court to punish a § 601 ward pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 213. The legislature intended to preserve intact the contempt powers of the juvenile court to enforce its lawful orders.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of habeas corpus requested by petitioner ward of the court. Under the applicable statutes, the juvenile court retained its inherent contempt powers to enforce its lawful orders, and, thus, the order confining petitioner in a secure facility during non-school hours for his contemptuous disobedience of a lawful court order that he attend school was properly imposed.

 

987 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Monroe


No. F004761


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


168 Cal. App. 3d 1205; 215 Cal. Rptr. 51; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2182



June 6, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied June 27, 1985. As Modified.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court for the Consolidated Fresno Judicial District of Fresno County, No. M 60952, James A. Ardaiz, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of child annoyance and molestation under Cal. Penal Code § 647a and contributing to the delinquency of a minor under Cal. Penal Code § 272, appealed a judgment of the Appellate Department of the Superior Court (California), that affirmed the denial of defendant's petition to strike the sex offender registration requirement of Cal. Penal Code § 290.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of child annoyance and molestation under Cal. Penal Code § 647a and contributing to the delinquency of a minor under Cal. Penal Code § 272. As a convicted sex offender he was required to register pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 290. Defendant filed a motion to strike the registration requirement which was denied by the trial court, and that denial was affirmed by the lower court. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment because the registration requirement for the offense defendant committed did not shock the conscience or offend fundamental notions of human dignity. The court held there was a rational basis for Cal Penal Code § 290; to wit: a legitimate state interest in controlling crime and preventing recidivism in sex offenders.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court that affirmed the denial of defendant's petition to strike the sex offender registration requirement was affirmed because the registration requirement of the state statute was constitutional.

 

988 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Russell


Crim. No. 43601.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


168 Cal. App. 3d 983; 214 Cal. Rptr. 412; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2159



May 31, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rev. den. Aug. 15, 1985, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A 621920, Rosemary M. Dunbar, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his first-degree murder conviction from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in that the murder was committed while engaged in the commission of a felony in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 189.


OVERVIEW: Appellant grabbed the victim as she left a bank, put a gun to her back, shot her in the heart, and took her purse. Appellant was convicted of murder in the first-degree in that the murder was committed while appellant was engaged in the commission of a felony in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 189. Appellant was sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of parole. Under Cal. Penal Code § 190.2, appellant received a sentence enhancement of two years. Defendant was to serve the life sentence without possibility of parole and then the two-year enhancement. Upon reconsideration, the court affirmed the conviction but modified the sentence enhancement. The court held that giving conflicting jury instructions concerning the special circumstance of intent to commit murder was harmless error. Appellant's intent was established by the evidence, and it was not reasonably probable that a jury could have reached a different verdict based upon a proper intent instruction. While the sentence enhancement under Cal. Penal Code § 12022.5 was proper, Cal. Penal Code § 669 required that appellant serve the two-year sentence before the indeterminate life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's felony murder conviction but modified the sentence enhancement. The court held that conflicting jury instructions concerning the special circumstance of intent to commit murder was harmless error. There was abundant evidence from which only the intent to kill could be inferred. While the sentence enhancement was proper, appellant was to serve the two year sentence before the indeterminate life sentence.

 

989 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Crissup


Crim. No. B003081.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


168 Cal. App. 3d 998; 214 Cal. Rptr. 623; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2161



May 31, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


*  At the direction of the court, and pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, the portion of the opinion certified for publication follows.


Rev. den. Aug. 22, 1985, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. CR 18182, James M. McNally, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which convicted him of six counts of issuing checks without sufficient funds for their payment in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 476a. The issue was whether § 476a was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged on six counts of issuing checks with insufficient funds for their payment in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 476a. A jury convicted defendant of all six counts and the trial judge sentenced him to one year in the county jail as a condition of five years' probation. Defendant appealed and claimed that § 476a was unconstitutionally vague because it did not prescribe the method to be used in formulating felony counts where a series of worthless checks exceeded $ 200. The court held that § 476a was constitutional but that the offenses had to be listed in chronological order. Here, the six felony counts did not list the checks in chronological order but instead, in an order permitting each count to total a sum as close to $ 200 as possible. The court found that the information therefore charged six felony counts whereas counts charging checks issued in chronological order would only provide five felony counts and one misdemeanor count. The convictions were modified to reflect this and, as modified, were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as modified to convict defendant of five felonies and one misdemeanor. The court found the statutory provision was constitutional but the trial court should have added the amounts of the worthless checks in chronological order, which is why the number, and type of convictions was modified.

Brown v. Cmty. Redevelopment Agency


Civ. No. 34067


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Three


168 Cal. App. 3d 1014; 214 Cal. Rptr. 626; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2163



May 31, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied August 15, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 403503, William R. Sheffield and Richard J. Beacom, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Respondent is entitled to costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which granted summary judgment for respondent Santa Ana Community Redevelopment Agency in plaintiff's action that contested, under the Government Spending Limitation, Cal. Const. art. XIII B, the issuance of tax allocation refunding bonds without prior voter approval.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer challenged the issuance of tax allocation refunding bonds by respondent Santa Ana Community Redevelopment Agency under the Community Redevelopment Law, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 33000 et seq., which permitted the agency to take advantage of increased property tax revenues in blighted areas without an increase in the tax scheme. Appellant's lawsuit challenged the validity of the bond issue claiming that it exceeded the agency's appropriations limit and required voter approval under the Government Spending Limitation, Cal. Const. art. XIII B. Respondent demurred and the trial court granted summary judgment for respondent. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that, in Cal. Health & Safety Code § 33678, the legislature had determined that redevelopment agencies' receipt of taxes pursuant to Cal. Const. art. XVI, § 16, were exempted from art. XIII B. The court noted that art. XIII B was vague and uncertain as applied to funding methods of redevelopment agencies, but that § 33678 was a legislative clarification of tax allocation financing which was neither arbitrary, unreasonable nor repugnant to the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment for respondent Santa Ana Community Redevelopment Agency because the legislature had specifically exempted respondent from the spending limits imposed by the constitutionally imposed government spending limitation, and the legislature's exemption was neither arbitrary, unreasonable, nor unconstitutional.

People v. Oliver


Crim. No. 42914


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


168 Cal. App. 3d 920; 214 Cal. Rptr. 587; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2152



May 30, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied August 29, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A622258, Edward M. Ross, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was found guilty of first degree murder, arson, and a special circumstance that he committed the murder while he committed the arson, by a jury and sentenced by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California). On appeal, defendant claimed that the jury instructions were improper, that the felony-murder rule under Cal. Penal Code § 189 was invalid, and that Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(a)(17)(iii) was defective and vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty and sentenced on charges of first degree murder, arson and the special circumstance that the murder was committed while he was committing arson. Appellant had thrown a Molotov cocktail into the window of a house attempting to kill his girlfriend, but the device set fire to the house, and a guest inside the house perished. On appeal, appellant brought nine assignments of error. The court held that the jury instructions appellant complained of were proper. It held that the felony murder rule under Cal. Penal Code § 189 was not anachronistic and did not violate appellant's constitutional rights. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 190.2 (a)(17)(viii) was not defective or unconstitutionally vague in its reference to arson under Cal. Penal Code § 447 because there was no section so numbered. The misdesignation did not make it impossible for the trial court to sentence appellant, and he was not prejudiced by the inaccuracy. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 190.2 did not impose cruel and unusual punishment because a life sentence without possibility of parole was not analogous to the death penalty. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. It held that the jury instructions complained of were proper, and that the felony murder rule was not anachronistic and did not violate appellant's constitutional rights. It held that a misdesignation in the number of the arson statute did not prejudice appellant, and that a life sentence without possibility of parole was not cruel and unusual punishment.

People v. Collins


Crim. No. 45088.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


168 Cal. App. 3d 839; 214 Cal. Rptr. 388; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2143



May 29, 1985 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rev. granted Aug. 30, 1985 (Crim. 24784)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A 625474, Madge S. Watai, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant of burglary in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 459 and issued a one-year sentence enhancement pursuant to Cal. Penal code § 667.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for burglary after police arrested him a few blocks from a burglary in possession of virtually all of the property subsequently identified as stolen. When approached by police, defendant attempted to dispose of a bag containing camera equipment he misidentified. Defendant stated that he was studying photography but could not identify the school where he was taking lessons. Defendant stated that his father gave him the camera equipment and that he purchased the equipment for $ 20. Defendant was serving a prison sentence for burglary and robbery and was on pass from a state prison halfway house when he was arrested. Defendant was convicted and given an enhanced sentence pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667.5(b). Upon review, the court affirmed the conviction but struck the enhanced sentence. The court held that defendant's actions prior to arrest corroborated his involvement in the burglary and that the trial court properly ruled that defendant's prior convictions could be used to impeach defendant. Defendant's enhanced sentence was improper because he had not yet completed a prior prison sentence as required by Cal. Penal Code § 667.5(g).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of burglary but struck a sentence enhancement. The court held that defendant's involvement in a burglary was corroborated by his attempt to dispose of the stolen property and by conflicting statements to police. Further, defendant's prior convictions could be used to impeach him if he chose to testify. The sentence enhancement was improper because defendant had not completed a prior prison sentence.

 

993 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Shippey


Crim. No. F003807


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


168 Cal. App. 3d 879; 214 Cal. Rptr. 553; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2147



May 29, 1985 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion certified.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 26536, Robert C. Deabenderfer, Judge. +


+ Assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded for new trial or dismissal of the charge at the option of the district attorney.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court of Kern County (California), where a jury convicted him of petty theft with a prior conviction for petty theft in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 666.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with petty theft with a prior conviction for petty theft in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 666. Defendant admitted the alleged prior petty theft conviction. Defendant was found guilty and sentenced to state prison for three years. He appealed and argued that the imposition of a three-year term of imprisonment for petty theft constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of Cal. Const. art. I, § 17. The court rejected defendant's argument because the facts did not entirely support defendant's analysis. The court held that proof of a prior conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 666 raised a misdemeanor crime punishable by a fine or county jail sentence to a felony punishable by imprisonment. The court reversed the conviction because defendant was neither advised of his constitutional right not to admit his prior petty theft or informed of the consequences of his admission, as required. The court held that it was reversible error because it was reasonably probable that defendant might not have admitted the prior conviction had he been so fully advised. Thus, the court reversed the conviction because prejudice to defendant resulted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for petty theft with a prior conviction for petty theft because defendant was neither advised of his constitutional rights not to admit his prior conviction nor informed of the consequences of his admission. This was reversible error because it was reasonably probable that defendant would not have admitted the prior conviction had he been so fully advised, and defendant was prejudiced by the admission.

Agric. Labor Relations Bd. v. Abatti Produce

Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One

OVERVIEW: Plaintiff Agricultural Labor Relations Board held that defendant produce company had illegally supported a decertification movement and engaged in an illegal refusal to bargain. The trial court issued a judgment enforcing plaintiff's decision and defendant appealed. 995 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Dalitz v. Penthouse Int'l


Civ. No. 69025


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


168 Cal. App. 3d 468; 214 Cal. Rptr. 254; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2109; 11 Media L. Rep. 2153



May 21, 1985 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - At the direction of the court, and pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, the portion of the opinion certified for publication follows.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The petition of defendants and appellants for review by the Supreme Court was denied September 19, 1985. Kaus, J., Broussard, J., and Grodin, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C124901, George M. Dell and Thomas Wilfred LeSage, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The summary judgment dismissing the cross-complaint of Penthouse (cross-appellant here) and in favor of Dalitz and Roen (cross-respondents here) as sanction for failure to obey the order of disclosure, is affirmed.

The cause is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed in the unpublished part of this opinion wherein we reverse the trial court's judgment dismissing appellants' complaint based on the court's order regarding the public-figure status of appellants.

Appellants cross-respondents Dalitz and Roen to recover their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant magazine sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed defendant's cross-action in libel and slander as a sanction for defendant's refusal to disclose the sources of an article it published which allegedly defamed plaintiff libelants who sought review of a judgment that they were public figures.


OVERVIEW: Defendant magazine published an article that alleged that plaintiff libelants were criminals. When plaintiffs filed an action in libel and slander, defendant cross-complained that plaintiffs defamed it. During discovery, defendant refused to reveal the sources of its story. In sanction, the trial court dismissed the cross-action. The trial court held against plaintiffs on the ground that, as public figures, they failed to prove malice. The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of defendant's cross-action but, in an unpublished portion of the opinion, reversed the judgment that plaintiffs were public figures. Dismissal of the cross-action was a proper sanction because, under Cal. Civ. Proc. § 2034(b), defendant was answerable for its reporters in agency. Defendant had only a qualified right to keep its sources confidential. Use of a five factor balancing test led to the conclusion that defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. I had to yield to the public interest in the ascertainment of truth in legal proceedings. Neither Cal. Const. art. I, § 2, Cal. Evid. Code § 1070, nor considerations of the sources' privacy barred narrowly-drawn disclosure provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of defendant magazine's libel cross-action because dismissal was a permissible sanction for defendant's refusal to disclose sources' identities as the privilege defendant enjoyed was qualified and subordinate to more compelling public interests. The court reversed the summary judgment entered against plaintiff libelants because they were not public figures.

People v. Poole


Crim. No. 15944


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


168 Cal. App. 3d 516; 214 Cal. Rptr. 502; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2113



May 21, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied August 29, 1985. Kaus, J., and Broussard, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR 66667, Robert P. McDonald and Robert C. Thaxton, Jr., Judges. *


* Assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which sentenced him after he pled guilty to robbery and attempted robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 211, 664 on the ground that he should be resentenced or be permitted to withdraw his plea because he had the right to be sentenced by the judge who accepted his plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to four counts of robbery, one count of attempted robbery, and admitted two prior prison terms pursuant to a plea bargain. He was sentenced to eight years in a state prison. The court affirmed defendant's sentence and held that defendant had implicitly acknowledged his right to be sentenced by the judge who accepted his plea when he agreed to be sentenced by another judge. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 2933's application to post-sentence imprisonment was constitutional and that defendant was not entitled to any credit for his pre-trial confinement. The court found that if there was any ambiguity in the imposition of consecutive sentences, the judge's clarification and transcript resolved the ambiguity. The court held that the "double-base-term" limit of Cal. Penal Code § 1170.1(g) was not an exception to Cal. Penal Code § 667's enhancement provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence and held that he waived his right to be sentenced by the judge who took his plea when he agreed to be sentenced by another judge. The court held that statutory enhancement of defendant's sentence was not limited by the "double-the-base term" rule, that the limitation of credits to post-sentence imprisonment was constitutionally valid, and that his eight-year sentence was reflected in the court's record.

Bd. of Police Comm'rs v. Superior Court


Civ. No. B005936


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


168 Cal. App. 3d 420; 214 Cal. Rptr. 493; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2105



May 20, 1985 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Good cause appearing, the superior court is hereby prohibited from taking any further action in this matter other than to vacate the order granting the preliminary injunction until the administrative remedies have been exhausted in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Board of Police Commissioners sought a writ of mandate challenging an order of respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which issued a preliminary injunction restraining petitioner from conducting a hearing to determine whether certain permits should be revoked.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner board of police commissioners granted a corporation, the real party in interest, a dance hall permit. Accusations were brought before petitioner charging the corporation with numerous violations of the Los Angeles Municipal Code. Respondent superior court granted the corporation a preliminary injunction. Petitioner sought a writ of mandate/prohibition charging that respondent superior court was without jurisdiction to act. The court granted the petition for a writ of prohibition and held that the superior court was prohibited from taking any further action in the matter other than to vacate its order until administrative remedies were exhausted. The court ruled that respondent was without jurisdiction to act, because petitioner had jurisdiction to hold its scheduled hearings on the accusations, and the corporation had not exhausted its administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner board of police commissioners' writ of mandate because respondent superior court was without jurisdiction to issue a preliminary injunction restraining petitioner from conducting a hearing regarding certain permits when administrative remedies were not exhausted.

People v. Traina


Crim. No. 13149


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


168 Cal. App. 3d 305; 214 Cal. Rptr. 213; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2095



May 16, 1985 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for partial publication - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, parts I, II, IV, V and VII, are not published.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 66255, Ronald Tochterman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which sentenced him to three years for a robbery conviction, Cal. Penal Code § 213, with an enhancement of five years for a prior robbery conviction. Cal. Penal Code § 667.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to robbery, Cal. Penal Code § 211 and the trial court found an allegation of a prior robbery conviction to be true. Defendant was sentenced to the middle term of three years for the robbery, Cal. Penal Code § 213, with an enhancement of five years for the prior conviction. Cal. Penal Code § 667 On appeal, defendant contended that because a prior robbery was punishable, for enhancement purposes, under both § 667 and Cal. Penal Code § 667.5, he should have had the benefit of the more favorable statute, § 667.5. The court affirmed and found that the critical element of a prior prison term was not specifically charged in the information, § 667 was applicable, and defendant was properly sentenced. Defendant also contended that the trial court improperly sentenced him to an aggregate term which exceeded twice his base term in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 1170.1(g) but the court found that the enhancement for defendant's prior robbery conviction was not subject to the double base limitation of § 1170.1(g).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that defendant could not be given the benefit of a more favorable enhancement statute because the critical element of a prior prison term was not charged nor was defendant's prior robbery conviction subject to a statutory sentencing limitation.

 

999 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



Sterling v. Santa Monica Rent Control Bd.


Civ. No. B003780


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


168 Cal. App. 3d 176; 214 Cal. Rptr. 71; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2081



May 15, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of plaintiff and respondent for review by the Supreme Court was denied August 21, 1985. Mosk, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. WEC080931, Laurence J. Rittenband, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the peremptory writ of prohibition is vacated. The superior court is directed to enter a new and different judgment consistent with the views expressed in this opinion and to issue a peremptory writ of prohibition only insofar as such may be consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Santa Monica Rent Control Board appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted a peremptory writ prohibiting defendant from utilizing all applicable criteria set forth in Santa Monica, Cal., Charter art. XVIII, § 1805(e), as bases upon which to adjust maximum rents downward and which ordered defendant to follow the trial court's judgment in all pending and future rent decrease cases.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Santa Monica Rent Control Board sought review of the trial court's judgment prohibiting defendant from basing decreases of a landlord's maximum allowable rent on all the factors set forth in Cal., Charter art. XVIII, § 1805(e). On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and vacated the peremptory writ that was issued against defendant. The court held that state law pertaining to the implied warranty of habitability, Cal. Civ. Code § 1942, and housing, health, and safety codes did not preempt defendant's authority to decrease maximum rents. The court ruled that conditions amounting to substantial deterioration or violations of housing, health, and safety codes could be considered as bases for rent decreases because they were relevant indicators of a landlord's comparative return on investment. The court held that defendant was also allowed to consider factors indicating a decrease in operating and maintenance expenses. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that defendant's decisions as to rent decreases were stayed pending final adjudication on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment prohibiting defendant Santa Monica Rent Control Board from considering substantial deterioration, violations of housing, health, and safety codes, or decreases in operating expenses as bases for rent decreases. The court held that state law did not preempt defendant's authority to decrease maximum rents and that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to decide issues with respect to other cases not before it.

 

1000 of 2274 DOCUMENTS



People v. Wooten


Crim. No. F003171


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


168 Cal. App. 3d 168; 214 Cal. Rptr. 36; 1985 Cal. App. LEXIS 2080



May 14, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Kern County, 25514, Marvin E. Ferguson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded for a hearing on the basis of the "flyer" described above.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County (California) that convicted him of violating Cal. Penal Code § 12025(a), (b) for carrying a concealed weapon on his person and carrying a concealed weapon in a vehicle, respectively. On appeal, defendant asserted, inter alia, that his vehicle came under the place of business exception to a permit per Cal. Penal Code § 12026 and that § 12026 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The police stopped defendant and found a pistol in his boot and other guns in his glove compartment. Upon the stop, the police used a flyer to allegedly identify him as part of a group involved in crime. A pat-down search was conducted. Defendant was convicted under Cal. Penal Code § 12025(a), (b) for carrying a concealed weapon on his person and carrying a concealed weapon in a vehicle, respectively. Defendant appealed the denial of his suppression motion and argued that Cal. Penal Code § 12026 was unconstitutionally vague and that his vehicle fell under the place of business exception granted by § 12026 for the permit requirement. The court reversed on the basis that a hearing was required on the sufficiency of the evidence to support the flyer. However, the court held that § 12026 was not unconstitutionally vague. The § 12026 exception did not apply to defendant's vehicle. The court held that anyone reading § 12026 would see that its exception for residences and places of business did not apply to vehicles used by every businessman that had to travel for business. The term place of business as used in § 12026, the statute granting the permit exception, meant a fixed location.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for a hearing on the sufficiency of the evidence for a flyer used for a pat-down search. The court held that the statute under which defendant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague. The court also held that the term place of business as used in the statute granting a permit exception meant a fixed location and did not apply to defendant's vehicle when used for bounty hunting.
